Well Evaluation
Marathon Oil Company
Donally 11-16H
Figure 1. H&P rig #438 drilling the Marathon Oil Company,
Donally 11-16H in Dunn County, North Dakota in August of 2014.
INTRODUCTION
The Marathon Oil Company, Donally 11-16H [SW SW Section 9, T146N, R93W; 401' FSL,
400' FWL] is to be drilled by Helmerich and Payne rig #438 and is located approximately 9.5
miles northeast of the town of Dunn Center in Dunn County, North Dakota (Figure 1). The
Donally 11-16H will be a dual section well, with an approximately 10,000' long lateral designed
to further oil production in the area. The surface will be drilled using fresh water drilling fluid,
while the vertical and curve sections will use diesel invert drilling fluid. Well plans called for
the vertical section to be drilled to a kick off point of 10,259' measured depth (MD). The curve
would then be built at a rate of 12.00º/100' and would land in the middle of the Middle Bakken
Member, target interval set by the Marathon Oil Company geologist. After casing the vertical
and curve, the lateral will be drilled using a salt-water drilling fluid. Geo-steering and
directional drilling techniques will be used to maintain maximum exposure to the target zone.
The planned lateral section was to be drilled south, at an azimuth of 182.14º. Upon anticipated
completion of the Donally 11-16H, the hole will be prepared for casing and production
evaluation. The hole will be lined and will use a 30 stage artificial fracture technique to
maximize the production value.
OFFSET WELLS
Three offset wells were used as primary controls while drilling the Donally 11-16H. Data
including gamma-ray signatures, from nearby offset wells were used to determine a prognosis of
formation tops. These wells include:
The Fleckenstein 21-16H [NE NW Section 16, T146N, R93W] which is located
approximately 0.25 miles southeast from the Donally 11-16H. This well was drilled
by Marathon Oil Company in May of 2008. It is a lateral, Middle Bakken well and is
currently active.
The Milton Guenther 14-9H [SW SW Section 9, T146N, R93W] which shares the
drilling pad with the Donally 11-16H. This well was drilled by Marathon Oil
Company in January and February of 2012. It is a lateral, Middle Bakken well and is
currently active.
The Lucy Fleckenstein 34-20H [SW SE Section 20, T146N, R93W] which is located
approximately 2 miles south-southwest from the Donally 11-16H. This well was
drilled by Marathon Oil Company in January of 2011. It is a lateral, Middle Bakken
well and is currently active.
The vicinity of these wells to the subject wells surface location made them ideal for developing a
well-rounded prognosis of formation tops. The Fleckenstein 21-16H and the Lucy Fleckenstein
34-20H were also used for structure control during the lateral (Figure 2).
ENGINEERING
The Donally 11-16H was spud on August 07, 2014 by H&P's rig #438. The surface hole was
drilled using a 13 ½" rock bit and 5" drill pipe to a depth of 2,275' MD, in 5.0 drilling hours. A
freshwater based drilling fluid was used during this operation. The surface hole was then
isolated using 57 joints of 9 " J-55 casing set to 2,260' MD and cemented to surface before
beginning the remaining vertical hole. The remaining vertical hole was started on August 09,
2014. Freshwater was displaced by invert diesel drilling fluid with mud weights fluctuating
between 9.75-10.00 pounds per gallon. Using one 8 ¾" Smith bit and one 8 ¾" Security bit the
vertical hole was truly maintained at a 2.3º inclination to the southwest using multiple magnetic
slides to reach a kick-off point (KOP) of 10,210' MD, in 53.8 drilling hours.
The curve build began on July 13, 2014. A new bottom-hole assembly (BHA) was built
including an 8 ¾" PDC Security bit, 2.12° fixed motor, and an MWD tool. The curve was
drilled to a total depth of 11,047' MD, in 9.7 drilling hours. 7" casing was then set to 11,032'
MD using 121 joints of HCL-80 set to 5,617' MD and 117 joints of P-110 set from 5,617' to
11,032' MD. The casing was then cemented prior to beginning the lateral section.
Diesel invert drilling fluid was displaced with a salt water based drilling fluid before beginning
the lateral on August 15, 2014. Mud weights were typically in the range of 9.75-10.00 pounds
per gallon. A 6" PDC Security bit was used along with a 1.40° fixed mud motor and an MWD
tool. This assembly was drilled to total depth in 66.4 drilling hours.
The Donally 11-16H reached a total depth of 21,055' MD on August 21, 2014, at a closure
direction of 182.02° and a true vertical depth (TVD) of 10,690.16'. The bottom-hole location is:
10,772.16' south and 380.83' west of the surface location or approximately 204.26' FSL and
21.20' FWL, SW SW Section 21, T146N, R93W.

GEOLOGIC EVALUATION
Methods
Geologic analysis for the Donally 11-16H was provided by two Sunburst Consulting well-site
geologists. Gas levels were monitored using a digital gas detector and chromatograph. The
chromatograph was interfaced with a Pason electronic data recorder. The Pason relayed data
such as measured depth, bit depth, and pump stroke information to the MController gas
monitoring software. MController returned gas in the form of total gas units (100 units = 1%
methane equivalent in air) to be logged and displayed across the drilling location. Multiple
component gases (ethane, methane, propane, and butane) and their concentrations were recorded
in parts per million. ¼" Poly-Flo ® tubing was used to direct gas into the chromatograph where
the data was then translated and lagged to the correct depth. Rig crews caught lagged samples,
in 30' intervals, under the supervision of well-site geologists. Analysis and evaluation of gas and
drill cuttings began in the Kibbey Formation at 8,370' MD and ended in the Middle Bakken
Member at 21,055'. Cuttings were observed in wet (isopropyl alcohol) and dry conditions under
a binocular microscope.
Lithology
Note: There were no electric logs run for the Donally 11-16H; all depths while drilling the
vertical and curve are referenced to driller's depth.
At the request of Marathon Oil Company, logging began 50-100' above the prognosis top of the
Kibbey "Lime", an interval of limestone within the Kibbey Formation.
The Kibbey Formation (Mississippian, Big Snowy Group) consists of red-orange siltstone with
some gray to red interbedded silty sandstone. There is a very distinct layer of limestone within
the Kibbey, referred to as the "Kibbey Lime", which was logged at 8,437' TVD (-5,956' MSL)
and consists of light to medium gray mudstone. There is a thin layer of anhydrite right above the
limestone that marks the top of the "Kibbey Lime" marker.
The Charles Formation (Mississippian, Madison Group) consists of limestone and a large
amount of evaporates including salt and anhydrite. The Charles First Salt was logged at 8,593'
TVD (-6,112' MSL), and often marks the top of the formation. The prospective Ratcliffe
interval is located below the Charles First Salt marker and was logged at 8,998' TVD (-6,517'
MSL).
The Mission Canyon Formation (Mississippian, Madison Group) consists of gray to brown
limestone and was logged at 9,270' TVD (-6,789' MSL). Some heavy gases were logged while
drilling in the Mission Canyon. Some areas also contain algae laminations, fossil fragments, and
trace amounts of intercrystalline porosity and dead oil stain.
The Lodgepole Formation (Mississippian, Madison Group) is characterized by light to medium
gray argillaceous limestone. The top was logged at 9,804' TVD (-7,323' MSL) and is marked by
a transition from limestone to argillaceous limestone. The "False Bakken" is a layer of shale
near the bottom of the Lodgepole Formation. It was logged at 10,651' TVD (-8,170' MSL). The
"Scallion" is a layer of limestone at the base of the
Lodgepole
Formation.
It
was
logged
at
10,660' TVD (-8,179' MSL). Several other
Lodgepole markers were also used to determine if a
change to the landing target was necessary.
The Bakken Formation (Devonian-Mississippian)
is comprised of two layers of black, petroliferous
shale and a mixed clastic and carbonate middle
member. The Upper Bakken Shale Member was
logged at 10,673' TVD (-8,192' MSL). This
member is recognized by its high gamma counts,
increase in rate of penetration (ROP), and typically
higher total gas units (Figure 3). The Middle Bakken
Figure 3. Wet cuttings of Upper Bakken
Member consists of three distinct lithologies and
Member, petroliferous shale (10x magnification).
was logged at 10,693' TVD (-8,212' MSL). A layer
of siltstone lies directly below the upper member. It is characterized by a gamma signature
ranging from 60-120 (API) counts and slower penetration rates than the shale. The siltstone is
typically gray with very fine intergranular porosity and spotty oil staining. Below the siltstone
lies a laterally discontinuous layer of fossiliferous (packstone) limestone. It is characterized by
abundant fossil fragments and a gamma signature ranging from 20-40 (API). Below the
limestone is a gray to brown silty sandstone, defined as the target zone (Figure 4). It has a gamma
signature ranging from 50-105 (API) counts. The top of the target was first logged at 10,707'
TVD (-8,226' MSL).
Figure 4. Wet cuttings of Middle Bakken silty sandstone (30x magnification).
Geo-steering
The well prognosis called for a landing target of 10,712' TVD at an inclination of 90°. The
landing target was set 20' below the base of the Upper Bakken Shale and 5' below the top of the
target area. Using gamma-ray data, well-site geologists were able to correlate formation tops
from the Donally 11-16H to nearby offset wells in the area to assure an accurate landing. No
changes were made to the prognosis landing target and the actual curve landing came in at
10,712' TVD, landing the well-bore 5' into the 10' target area.
Gamma-ray readings were typically 50-95 (API) counts while in target. The location of the
target area put the top of the target 15' below the base of the Upper Bakken Shale Member and
the base of the target 12' above the top of the Lower Bakken Shale Member, making the Middle
Bakken Member approximately 37' thick.
The middle Bakken target zone was entered at approximately 10,947' MD (10,707' TVD). The
well-bore was maintained in the target zone for 82% of the lateral. The formation rose 17.6' of
TVD, over the course of the lateral, resulting in a gross apparent dip of +0.10° (Figure 5).

Gas and Oil Show
The label used to quantify gas for this well was units (100 units is equal to 1% methane
equivalent in air). The first time any significant gas was logged was a gas show while drilling of
25 units in the Kibbey Formation. There were multiple gas shows from 13-95 units logged
during vertical drilling. Gas increased substantially just below the False Bakken, and included a
trip gas show of 2,686 units observed while circulating after the curve landing. There were
multiple gas shows around 100-2,000 units from the False Bakken to the curve landing, likely
due to fracture porosity.
Background gas in the lateral ranged from 2,000 to 4,000 units. Higher gas levels were observed
from 14,350'-16,090' MD and 19,850'-21,055' MD possibly due to crossing of fracture porosity
or increased intergranular porosity. Poor quality drilling mud and salt water transfers lead to low
and sometimes erratic gas readings throughout the lateral. Occasional to common amounts of
yellow-brown oil were observed over the shakers and in the sample wash. The highest gas show
in the lateral was a connection gas show of 4,835 units and was logged at 14,463' MD.
Gas was circulated through the gas buster entirely starting at 11,587' MD, and an intermittent 3-
25' flare was observed. Occasionally a 2-8' continuous flare was observed. No back pressure
was held while drilling the Donally 11-16H (Figure 6).

SUMMARY
The Marathon Oil Company, Donally 11-16H is a Middle Bakken Member, lateral well located
north of the town of Dunn Center in Dunn County, North Dakota. It was spud on August 7, 2014
and was drilled to a kick off point of 10,210' MD. The curve was landed at 10,712' TVD, 5'
into the targeted silty sandstone. The target interval contained fine intergranular porosity and
trace to rare amounts of light brown oil staining. Background gas in the lateral ranged from
2,000-4,000 units, with gas shows as high as 4,835 units. Throughout the lateral there were
occasional to common amounts of yellow-brown oil over the shakers and in the sample wash.
The well-bore was maintained within the target interval for 82% of the 10,185' lateral section,
along a 0.10° up dip. The Donally 11-16H reached a total depth of 21,055' MD on August 21,
2014 after 14 drilling days.
Respectfully Submitted,
Nicholas R. Higgins

LITHOLOGY
Rig crews caught lagged samples in 30' intervals under the supervision of Sunburst geologists. A
detailed list of sampling intervals is included in the well data summary page. Sample or gamma-ray
marker tops have been inserted in the sample descriptions below for reference. Samples were
examined wet and dry under a binocular microscope. The drilling fluid was diesel-based invert from
surface casing to 11,047' MD, and changed to salt water from 11,047' to 21,055' (TD). Sample
collection began at 8,370' MD.
Drilling in the Kibbey Formation [Big Snowy Group]
8370-8400 SILTSTONE: red-brown, trace orange-brown and light brown, soft to friable, blocky, calcite cemented,
poorly cemented, sandy in part; rare SILTY SANDSTONE: off white to tan, fine grained, friable, sub-rounded,

Dear William:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 24406, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The approval is
granted on the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement, shall be located approximately down the
north-south axis (500' drilling corridor per Commission policy) and be no closer than the 200' setback from the north &
south boundaries within the 2560 acre spacing unit consisting of Sections 16, 17, 20 & 21 T146N R93W.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: Effective June 1, 2014, a covered leak-proof container (with placard) for filter sock
disposal must be maintained on the well site beginning when the well is spud, and must remain on-site during
clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations are conducted.
MARATHON OIL
COMPANY must take into consideration NDAC 43-02-03-28 (Safety Regulation) when contemplating
simultaneous operations on the above captioned location. Pursuant to NDAC 43-02-03-28 (Safety Regulation) "No
boiler, portable electric lighting generator, or treater shall be placed nearer than 150 feet to any producing well or
oil tank." In cases where a spacing unit is accessed from an off-site drill pad, an affidavit must be provided
affirming that the surface owner of the multi-well pad agrees to accept burial on their property of the cuttings
generated from drilling the wells into an offsite spacing unit. MARATHON OIL CO must contact NDIC Field
Inspector Ashleigh Devenberg at 701-290-3277prior to location construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well drilling and
completion operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will prevent pollution of
the land surface and freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits are prohibited. All pits shall be
inspected by an authorized representative of the director prior to lining and use. Drill cuttings and solids must be stabilized
in a manner approved by the director prior to placement in a cuttings pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC. The
proposed directional plan is at a legal location. The minimum legal coordinates from the well head at casing point are: 601 S
& 150 W. Also, based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum legal coordinate from the well head is: 10776 S.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the approved
drilling permit on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to commence before the 3rd
business day following publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may be waived by the Director.
Application for a waiver must be by sworn affidavit providing the information necessary to evaluate the extenuating
circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and any other information that would allow the Director to
conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the drilling permit, the applicant should retain the permit.
William F Groffy

upon the spudding of the well. This information should be relayed to the Oil & Gas Division, Bismarck, via telephone. The

Well name, legal location, permit number, drilling contractor, company

Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a message if after hours or on the weekend.
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey contractor shall
file a certified copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion. Surveys must be
submitted as one electronic copy, or in a form approved by the director. However, the director may require the directional
survey to be filed immediately after completion if the survey is needed to conduct the operation of the director's office in a
timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one adobe document, with a certification cover page to
certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve (or when
sliding) and 90 feet in the lateral.
Confidential status
Your request for confidential status of all information furnished to the Director, or his representatives, is hereby
granted. Such information, except production runs, shall remain confidential for six months commencing on the date the
well is spud.
Confidential status notwithstanding, the Director and his representatives shall have access to all well records wherever
located. Your company personnel, or any person performing work for your company shall permit the Director and his
representatives to come upon any lease, property, well, or drilling rig operated or controlled by them, complying with all
safety rules, and to inspect the records and operation of such wells and to have access at all times to any and all records of
wells. The Commission's field personnel periodically inspect producing and drilling wells. Any information regarding such
wells shall be made available to them at any time upon request. The information so obtained by the field personnel shall be
maintained in strict confidence and shall be available only to the Commission and its staff.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12 hours, and tail
cement utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi before drilling the plug or
initiating tests.
Logs
NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and
porosity zones can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well bore, and
(3) a log from which the presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic cement evaluation
log) in every well in which production or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior to completing the well.
All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as one digital TIFF (tagged image file format) copy and one digital LAS (log
ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a standard CD, DVD, or attached to an email sent to
digitallogs@nd.gov Thank you for your cooperation.

RE: Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director
Marathon Oil Company

BOP EQUIPMENT
Marathon Oil Company's minimum specifications for pressure
control equipment are as follows:
Ram Type:
13 5/8" 5000 psi blind, pipe and annular.
a. Due to Marathon's experience it is felt that the above
referenced BOP equipment is adequate for drilling this well.
The reduced permeability of the target zone along with
Marathon's area experience of drilling over 250 horizontal
wells indicate that a MASP of 3000 psi is more adjusted to
the reality of the reservoir.
BOP and other equipment testing:
a. Floor valve, dart valve, kill valves, check valve, manual
choke line valve, manual top drive valve, hydraulic top
drive valve, HCR, choke house valves, choke manifold,
choke hose, choke line, kill line, upper pipe rams, lower
pipe rams, blind rams (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min. High
Test: 5000 psi x 10 min.)
b. Annular Preventer (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min. High Test:
2500 psi x 10 min.)
c. Rotating head and Orbit Valve (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min.
High Test: 1500 psi x 10 min.)
Frequency:
a. After initial installation (NU BOPE).
b. Whenever any seal subject to test pressure is broken.
c. After any repairs compromising seal.
d. At 30-day intervals.
All other equipment (upper and lower Kelly cocks, IBOP,
etc) will be tested according to Onshore Oil and Gas
Order No. 2.

Gas Capture Plan
Donally 11-16H

Map of Well-site
The Donally 11-16H
wellhead will be located
on the Sydney Pad with
two new wells and one
existing well:
Milton Guenther 14-9H
Sydney 14-9TFH
VMR Trust 11-16TFH
Page 2 of 3
Gas Capture Plan
Donally 11-16H
Sec 9 T146N R93W
Field: Bailey
Flowback Strategy
Anticipated First Production date
The well is expected to commence production around December 2014. It is anticipated that it will be connected to
a gas sales pipeline at first production.
Multi-well startup
The well is expected to flowback concurrently with one of the other wells on the Sydney location. Flowback of the
well is expected to be approximately 4-10 days in duration.
Anticipated Oil and Gas Rates
Average Gas rate from the well during flowback is anticipated to be around 500 MSCFD.
Average Gas Rate from the wellpad during flowback is anticipated to be around 1,200 MSCFD
Average Oil Rate from the well during flowback is anticipated to be around 900 bopd
Average Oil Rate from the wellpad during flowback is anticipated to be between around 1,800 bopd
System Capacity and Utilization
Existing Gas Line
Capacity (MMSCFD)
Throughput (MMSCFD)
Current
2.5 MMSCFD
2 MMSCFD

1.1 MMSCFD (w/o new
6 MMSCFD
well)
Gas Gatherer Expansion Plans
16" line will connect Killdeer and Lost Bridge Compressor stations allowing gas to flow to Oneok Garden Creek

Oneok Garden Creek II / III Gas Processing facilities ­ Q3 2014 / Q1 2015

Alternatives to flaring
Use of gas on lease, including fuel gas for Heater Treaters, is an alternative to flaring that is intended for this
location as well as connection to a gas pipeline.
Other alternatives to flaring are noted in NDIC order 24665.

requirements.
